<div class="video-wrapper-left">
  <iframe class="devsite-embedded-youtube-video" data-video-id="haMOUb3KVSo"

  </iframe>

<div class="video-wrapper">

<p>Remember, when you structure your data in <span class="notranslate">Cloud Firestore</span>, you
have a few different options:
<ul style="list-style: disc outside">
  <li>Documents</li>
  <li>Multiple collections</li>
  <li>Subcollections within documents</li>
</ul>
  <p>Consider the advantages of each option as they
    relate to your use case. A few example structures for hierarchical data
  are outlined in this guide.</p></p>

<h3 id="nested_data_in_documents" data-text="Nested data in documents" tabindex="-1">Nested data in documents</h3>

<p>You can nest complex objects like arrays or maps within documents.</p>

<table>
<tr>
<td>
<ul>
<li><strong>Advantages:</strong> If you have simple, fixed lists of data that
you want to keep within your documents, this is easy to set up and streamlines
your data structure.</li>
<li>
<strong>Limitations:</strong>
This isn't as scalable as other options,
especially if your data expands over time. With larger or growing lists, the
document also grows, which can lead to slower document retrieval times.
</li>
<li><strong>What's a possible use case?</strong> In a chat app, for example, you
might store a user's 3 most recently visited chat rooms as a nested list in
their profile.
</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:35%">
<ul><li> <span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span> alovelace<br />
<ul><li>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;name :<br />
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;first : "Ada"<br/>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;last : "Lovelace"<br/>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;born : 1815<br/>
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rooms :<br />
      &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0 : "Software Chat"<br/>
      &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;1 : "Famous Figures"<br/>
      &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2 : "Famous SWEs"<br/>
      </li>
      </ul>
</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>

<h3 id="subcollections" data-text="Subcollections" tabindex="-1">Subcollections</h3>

<p>You can create collections within documents when you have data that might expand
over time.</p>

<table>
<tr>
<td>
<ul>
<li><strong>Advantages:</strong> As your lists grow, the size of the parent
document doesn't change. You also get full query capabilities on subcollections,
and you can issue <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/firestore/query-data/queries">
collection group queries</a> across subcollections.
</li>
<li>
<strong>Limitations:</strong> You can't easily delete subcollections.
</li>
<li><strong>What's a possible use case?</strong> In the same chat app, for
example, you might create collections of users or messages within chat room
documents.
</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:35%">
<ul>
<li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">collections_bookmark</span> science
    <ul><li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span> software<br />
        &nbsp;&nbsp;name : "software chat"
        <ul><li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">collections_bookmark</span>
        users
            <ul><li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span>
            alovelace<br />
                &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;first : "Ada"<br/>
                &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;last : "Lovelace"<br/>
                </li>

            <li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span>
            sride<br />
               &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;first : "Sally"<br/>
                &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;last : "Ride"`</li>
                </ul>
                </li>
                </ul><br/><br/>
   <li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span> astrophysics
        <ul><li>...<br/></li></ul>
        </li>
</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>

<h3 id="root-level_collections" data-text="Root-level collections" tabindex="-1">Root-level collections</h3>

<p>Create collections at the root level of your database to organize disparate data
sets.</p>

<table>
<tr>
<td>
<ul>
<li><strong>Advantages:</strong> Root-level collections are good for many-to-many
relationships and provide powerful querying within each collection.
</li>
<li>
<strong>Limitations:</strong> Getting data that is naturally hierarchical might
become increasingly complex as your database grows.
</li>
<li><strong>What's a possible use case?</strong> In the same chat app,
for example, you might create one collection for users and another for rooms and
messages.
</li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:35%">
<ul> <li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">collections_bookmark</span>
    users
    <ul><li> <span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span> alovelace<br/>
        &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;first : "Ada"<br/>
        &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;last : "Lovelace"<br/>
        &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;born : 1815<br/>
        </li>
        <li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span> sride<br/>
        &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;first : "Sally"<br/>
        &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;last : "Ride"<br/>
        &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;born : 1951<br/>
        </li>
        </ul>
        </li>

<li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">collections_bookmark</span> rooms
    <ul><li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span> software
        <ul><li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">collections_bookmark</span>
        messages
            <ul><li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span>
            message1<br />
                &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from : "alovelace"<br/>
                &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;content : "..."<br/>
                </li>
           <li><span class="material-icons notranslate" aria-hidden="true" translate="no">class</span>
            message2<br/>
                &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from : "sride"<br/>
                &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;content : "..."<br/>
                </li>
                </ul>
                </li>
                </ul>
                </li>
                </ul>
                </li>
                </ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
